envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n     4→\n     5→import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n     6→import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n     7→import   16→\n    17→option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n    18→option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n    19→option java_multiple_files = true;\n    20→option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n    21→option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n    22→\n    23→// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n    24→// External Processing Filter\n    25→// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n    26→\n    27→// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n    28→\n    29→// **Current Implementation Status:**\n    30→// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n    31→//\n    32→// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n    33→\n    34→// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n    35→// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n    36→//\n    37→// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n    38→// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n    39→// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n    40→// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n    41→//\n    42→// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n    43→// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n    44→// and how it should be processed.\n    45→//\n    46→// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n    47→//\n    48→// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n    49→// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n    50→// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n    51→//   sent asynchronously.\n    52→// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n    53→//\n    54→// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n    55→// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n    56→// processor must send a matching response.\n    57→//\n    58→// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n    59→// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n    60→//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n    61→//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n    62→// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n    63→//   to SEND.\n    64→// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n    65→//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n    66→//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n    67→// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n    68→// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n    69→//   request trailers.\n    70→//\n    71→// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n    72→// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n    73→// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n    74→// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    75→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    76→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    77→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    78→//\n    79→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    80→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    81→//\n    82→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    83→//   on the content of the headers.\n    84→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    85→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    86→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    87→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    88→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    89→//\n    90→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    91→// server\n    92→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    93→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    94→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    95→//\n    96→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    97→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    98→// name.\n    99→//\n   100→// [#next-free-field: 18]\n   101→message ExternalProcessor {\n   102→  reserved 4;\n   103→\n   104→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   105→\n   106→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   107→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   108→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   109→\n   110→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   111→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n   112→  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n   113→  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n   114→  // downstream client will be reset.\n   115→  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n   116→  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n   117→  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n   118→\n   119→  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n   120→  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n   121→  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n   122→\n   123→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   124→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   125→  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n   126→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n   127→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   128→  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n   129→\n   130→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   131→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   132→  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n   133→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   134→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   135→  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n   136→\n   137→  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n   138→  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n   139→  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n   140→  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n   141→  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n   142→  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n   143→  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n   144→  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n   145→  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n   146→    lte {seconds: 3600}\n   147→    gte {}\n   148→  }];\n   149→\n   150→  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n   151→  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n   152→  string stat_prefix = 8;\n   153→\n   154→  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n   155→  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n   156→  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n   157→  // with the header prefix set via\n   158→  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n   159→  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n   160→  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n   161→  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. = \"proto3\";\n\npackage envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n\nimport \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n\nimport \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\nimport \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n\nimport \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\nimport \"validate/validate.proto\";\n\noption java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\noption java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\noption java_multiple_files = true;\noption go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\noption (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n\n// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 18]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n\n  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n  // with the header prefix set via\n  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n  // route to be recomputed, set the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field to true in the same response.\n  config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n\n  // Specify the upper bound of\n  // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n  // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field is set in an external processor response.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n\n  // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n  // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n\n  // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n  // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n  // ext_proc filter name.\n  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n\n  // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n  // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n  // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n  // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n\n  // If set to true, ignore the\n  // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n  // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n  // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n  // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n\n  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n  // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n  //\n  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n  //\n  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n  // This also means that\n  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n  //\n  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n  //\n  // .. warning::\n  //\n  //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n  //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n  //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n  //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n  //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n  //\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n}\n\n// The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n// dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n// metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\nmessage MetadataOptions {\n  message MetadataNamespaces {\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n    repeated string untyped = 1;\n\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\n    // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\n    // definition for safe parsing.\n    repeated string typed = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\n  // the external processing server.\n  MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\n  // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n  // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n  MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n}\n\n// The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n// allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n//\n// This works as below:\n//\n//   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n//   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n//      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n//      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n//      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\nmessage HeaderForwardingRules {\n  // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n  // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\n  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\n\n  // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n  // processing server. A set of\n    // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n    // flag set in a less-specific one.\n    ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n  }\n}\n\n// Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n// [#next-free-field: 8]\nmessage ExtProcOverrides {\n  // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n  bool async_mode = 2;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n  // ``request_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n  // ``response_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n\n  // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n  // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n  // config used. [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n    25→// External Processing Filter\n    26→// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n    27→\n    28→// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n    29→\n    30→// **Current Implementation Status:**\n    31→// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n    32→//\n    33→// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n    34→\n    35→// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n    36→// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n    37→//\n    38→// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n    39→// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n    40→// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n    41→// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n    42→//\n    43→// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n    44→// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n    45→// and how it should be processed.\n    46→//\n    47→// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n    48→//\n    49→// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n    50→// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n    51→// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n    52→//   sent asynchronously.\n    53→// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n    54→//\n    55→// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n    56→// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n    57→// processor must send a matching response.\n    58→//\n    59→// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n    60→// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n    61→//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n    62→//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n    63→// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n    64→//   to SEND.\n    65→// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n    66→//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n    67→//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n    68→// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n    69→// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n    70→//   request trailers.\n    71→//\n    72→// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n    73→// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n    74→// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n    75→// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    76→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    77→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    78→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    79→//\n    80→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    81→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    82→//\n    83→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    84→//   on the content of the headers.\n    85→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    86→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    87→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    88→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    89→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    90→//\n    91→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    92→// server\n    93→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    94→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    95→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    96→//\n    97→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    98→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    99→// name.\n   100→//\n   101→// [#next-free-field: 20]\n   102→message ExternalProcessor {\n   103→  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n   104→  // is received in response to request headers.\n   105→  enum RouteCacheAction {\n   106→    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n   107→    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   108→    // field is set in an external processor response.\n   109→    DEFAULT = 0;\n   110→\n   111→    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   112→    // the external processor response.\n   113→    CLEAR = 1;\n   114→\n   115→    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   116→    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n   117→    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n   118→    // to true.\n   119→    RETAIN = 2;\n   120→  }\n   121→\n   122→  reserved 4;\n   123→\n   124→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   125→\n   126→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   127→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   128→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   129→\n   130→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   131→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n   132→  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n   133→  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n   134→  // downstream client will be reset.\n   135→  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n   136→  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n   137→  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n   138→\n   139→  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n   140→  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n   141→  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n   142→\n   143→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   144→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   145→  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n   146→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n   147→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   148→  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n   149→\n   150→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   151→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   152→  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n   153→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   154→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   155→  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n   156→\n   157→  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n   158→  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n   159→  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n   160→  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n   161→  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n   162→  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n   163→  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n   164→  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n   165→  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n   166→    lte {seconds: 3600}\n   167→    gte {}\n   168→  }];\n   169→\n   170→  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n   171→  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n   172→  string stat_prefix = 8;\n   173→\n   174→  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n   175→  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n   176→  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n   177→  // with the header prefix set via\n   178→  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n   179→  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n   180→  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n   181→  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n   182→  // route to be recomputed, set the\n   183→  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   184→  // field to true in the same response.\n   185→  config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n   186→\n   187→  // Specify the upper bound of\n   188→  // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n   189→  // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n   190→  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n   191→    lte {seconds: 3600}\n   192→    gte {}\n   193→  }];\n   194→\n   195→  // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n   196→  // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n   197→  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n   198→\n   199→  // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n   200→  // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n   201→  // ext_proc filter name.\n   202→  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n   203→\n   204→  // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n   205→  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n   206→  // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n   207→  // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n   208→  // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n   209→  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n   210→\n   211→  // If set to true, ignore the\n   212→  // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n   213→  // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n   214→  // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n   215→  // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n   216→  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n   217→\n   218→  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n   219→  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n   220→\n   221→  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n   222→  // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n   223→  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n   224→  //\n   225→  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n   226→  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n   227→  //\n   228→  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n   229→  // This also means that\n   230→  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n   231→  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n   232→  //\n   233→  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n   234→  //\n   235→  // .. warning::\n   236→  //\n   237→  //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n   238→  //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n   239→  //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n   240→  //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n   241→  //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n   242→  //\n   243→  bool observability_mode = 17;\n   244→\n   245→  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n   246→  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   247→  // field is set in an external processor response.\n   248→  // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\n   249→  // It is recommended to set ``route_cache_action`` which supersedes ``disable_clear_route_cache``.\n   250→  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n   251→      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n   252→\n   253→  // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response is\n   254→  // received in response to request headers. It is recommended to set this field than set\n   255→  // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`.\n   256→  // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\n   257→  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n   258→      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n   259→\n   260→  // Specifies the deferred closure timeout for gRPC stream that connects to external processor. Currently, the deferred stream closure\n   261→  // is only used in :ref:`observability_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`.\n   262→  // In observability mode, gRPC streams may be held open to the external processor longer than the lifetime of the regular client to\n   263→  // backend stream lifetime. In this case, Envoy will eventually timeout the external processor stream according to this time limit.\n   264→  // The default value is 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if not specified.\n   265→  google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n   266→}\n   267→\n   268→// The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n   269→// dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n   270→// metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\n   271→message MetadataOptions {\n   272→  message MetadataNamespaces {\n   273→    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n   274→    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n   275→    repeated string untyped = 1;\n   276→\n   277→    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n   278→    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\n   279→    // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\n   280→    // definition for safe parsing.\n   281→    repeated string typed = 2;\n   282→  }\n   283→\n   284→  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\n   285→  // the external processing server.\n   286→  MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\n   287→\n   288→  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\n   289→  // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n   290→  // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n   291→  MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n   292→}\n   293→\n   294→// The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n   295→// allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n   296→//\n   297→// This works as below:\n   298→//\n   299→//   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n   300→//   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n   301→//      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n   302→//   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n   303→//      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n   304→//   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n   305→//      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n   306→message HeaderForwardingRules {\n   307→  // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n   308→  // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\n   309→  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\n   310→\n   311→  // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n   312→  // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\n   313→  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\n   314→}\n   315→\n   316→// Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\n   317→// virtual host or cluster.\n   318→message ExtProcPerRoute {\n   319→  oneof override {\n   320→    option (validate.required) = true;\n   321→\n   322→    // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\n   323→    // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\n   324→    bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\n   325→\n   326→    // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\n   327→    // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n   328→    // flag set in a less-specific one.\n   329→    ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n   330→  }\n   331→}\n   332→\n   333→// Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n   334→// [#next-free-field: 8]\n   335→message ExtProcOverrides {\n   336→  // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n   337→  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n   338→\n   339→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   340→  // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n   341→  bool async_mode = 2;\n   342→\n   343→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   344→  // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n   345→  // ``request_attributes`` field.\n   346→  repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n   347→\n   348→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   349→  // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n   350→  // ``response_attributes`` field.\n   351→  repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n   352→\n   353→  // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n   354→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n   355→\n   356→  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n   357→  // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n   358→  // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n   359→  // config used. It is the prerogative of the control plane to ensure this\n   360→  // most-specific config contains the correct final overrides.\n   361→  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 6;\n   362→\n   363→  // Additional metadata to include into streams initiated to the ext_proc gRPC\n   364→  // service. This can be used for scenarios in which additional ad hoc\n   365→  // authorization headers (e.g. ``x-foo-bar: baz-key``) are to be injected or\n   366→  // when a route needs to partially override inherited metadata.\n   367→  repeated config.core.v3.HeaderValue grpc_initial_metadata = 7;\n   368→}\n   369→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. ACTIVE;\n\n// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 20]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n  // is received in response to request headers.\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n    // field is set in an external processor response.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response.\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n    // to true.\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. By default, request and response headers are sent,\n    // while trailers are skipped.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Send the header or trailer.\n    SEND = 1;\n\n    // Do not send the header or trailer.\n    SKIP = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Control how the request and response bodies are handled\n  // When body mutation by external processor is enabled, ext_proc filter will always remove\n  // the content length header in three cases below because content length can not be guaranteed\n  // to be set correctly:\n  // 1) STREAMED BodySendMode: header processing completes before body mutation comes back.\n  // 2) BUFFERED_PARTIAL BodySendMode: body is buffered and could be injected in different phases.\n  // 3) BUFFERED BodySendMode + SKIP HeaderSendMode: header processing (e.g., update content-length) is skipped.\n  //\n  // In Envoy's http1 codec implementation, removing content length will enable chunked transfer\n  // encoding whenever feasible. Envoy sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n    29→// 2. The service sends back a ProcessingResponse message that directs Envoy\n    30→//    to either stop processing, continue without it, or send it the\n    31→//    next chunk of the message body.\n    32→// 3. If so requested, Envoy sends the server chunks of the message body,\n    33→//    or the entire body at once. In either case, the server sends back\n    34→//    a ProcessingResponse after each message it receives.\n    35→// 4. If so requested, Envoy sends the server the HTTP trailers,\n    36→//    and the server sends back a ProcessingResponse.\n    37→// 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again\n    38→//    at step 1 when Envoy receives a response from the upstream server.\n    39→// 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly,\n    40→//    then Envoy proceeds without consulting the server.\n    41→// 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error,\n    42→//    then Envoy returns a 500 error to the client, unless the filter\n    43→//    was configured to ignore errors.\n    44→//\n    45→// In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but\n    46→// using a gRPC stream to make it easier for the server to\n    47→// maintain state.\n    48→\n    49→service ExternalProcessor {\n    50→  // This begins the bidirectional stream that Envoy will use to\n    51→  // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\n    52→  // protocol is described by the ProcessingRequest and ProcessingResponse\n    53→  // messages below.\n    54→  rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\n    55→  }\n    56→}\n    57→\n    58→// This represents the different types of messages that Envoy can send\n    59→// to an external processing server.\n    60→// [#next-free-field: 11]\n    61→message ProcessingRequest {\n    62→  reserved 1;\n    63→\n    64→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n    65→\n    66→  // Each request message will include one of the following sub-messages. Each entry\n   110→  // in the list is populated from the standard\n   111→  // :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>` supported across Envoy.\n   112→  map<string, google.protobuf.Struct> attributes = 9;\n   113→\n   114→  // Specify whether the filter that sent this request is running in :ref:`observability_mode\n   115→  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`\n   116→  // and defaults to false.\n   117→  //\n   118→  // * A value of ``false`` indicates that the server must respond\n   119→  //   to this message by either sending back a matching ProcessingResponse message,\n   120→  //   or by closing the stream.\n   121→  // * A value of ``true`` indicates that the server should not respond to this message, as any\n   122→  //   responses will be ignored. Envoy sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n// 2. The service sends back a ProcessingResponse message that directs Envoy\n//    to either stop processing, continue without it, or send it the\n//    next chunk of the message body.\n// 3. If so requested, Envoy sends the server chunks of the message body,\n//    or the entire body at once. In either case, the server sends back\n//    a ProcessingResponse after each message it receives.\n// 4. If so requested, Envoy sends the server the HTTP trailers,\n//    and the server sends back a ProcessingResponse.\n// 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again\n//    at step 1 when Envoy receives a response from the upstream server.\n// 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly,\n//    then Envoy proceeds without consulting the server.\n// 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error,\n//    then Envoy returns a 500 error to the client, unless the filter\n//    was configured to ignore errors.\n//\n// In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but\n// using a gRPC stream to make it easier for the server to\n// maintain state.\n\nservice ExternalProcessor {\n  // This begins the bidirectional stream that Envoy will use to\n  // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\n  // protocol is described by the ProcessingRequest and ProcessingResponse\n  // messages below.\n  rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\n  }\n}\n\n// This represents the different types of messages that Envoy can send\n// to an external processing server.\n// [#next-free-field: 11]\nmessage ProcessingRequest {\n  reserved 1;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Each request message will include one of the following sub-messages. Unless ``observability_mode`` is true, the server must send back\n    // a BodyResponse message, an ImmediateResponse message, or close the stream.\n    HttpBody request_body = 4;\n\n    // A chunk of the HTTP response body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back\n    // a BodyResponse message or close the stream.\n    HttpBody response_body = 5;\n\n    // The HTTP trailers for the request path. However, it may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages\n  //   are needed.\n  //\n  bool observability_mode = 10;\n}\n\n// For every ProcessingRequest received by the server with the ``observability_mode`` field\n// set to false, the server must send back exactly one ProcessingResponse message.\n// [#next-free-field: 11]\nmessage ProcessingResponse {\n  oneof response {\n    option (validate.required) = true;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with the\n    // ``request_headers`` field set.\n    HeadersResponse request_headers = 1;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with the\n    // ``response_headers`` field set.\n    HeadersResponse response_headers = 2;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``request_body`` field set.\n    BodyResponse request_body = 3;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``response_body`` field set.\n    BodyResponse response_body = 4;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``request_trailers`` field set.\n    TrailersResponse request_trailers = 5;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``response_trailers`` field set.\n    TrailersResponse response_trailers = 6;\n\n    // If specified, attempt to create a locally generated response, send it\n    // downstream, and stop processing additional filters and ignore any\n    // additional messages received from the remote server for this request or\n    // response. If a response has already started -- for example, if this\n    // message is sent response to a ``response_body`` message -- then\n    // this will either ship the reply directly to the downstream codec,\n    // or reset the stream.\n    ImmediateResponse immediate_response = 7;\n  }\n\n  // Optional metadata that will be emitted as dynamic metadata to be consumed by\n  // following filters. This is the default.\n    CONTINUE = 0;\n\n    // Apply the specified header mutation, replace the body with the body\n    // specified in the body mutation (if present), and do not send any\n    // further messages for this request or response even if the processing\n    // mode is configured to do so.\n    //\n    // When used in response to a request_headers or response_headers message,\n    // this status makes it possible to either completely replace the body\n    // while discarding the original body, or to add a body to a message that\n    // formerly did not have one.\n    //\n    // In other words, this response makes it possible to turn an HTTP GET\n    // into a POST, PUT, or PATCH.\n    CONTINUE_AND_REPLACE = 1;\n  }\n\n  // If set, provide additional direction on how the Envoy proxy should\n  // handle the rest of the HTTP filter chain.\n  ResponseStatus status = 1 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // Instructions on how to manipulate the headers. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again\n//    at step 1 when Envoy receives a response from the upstream server.\n// 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly,\n//    then Envoy proceeds without consulting the server.\n// 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error,\n//    then Envoy returns a 500 error to the client, unless the filter\n//    was configured to ignore errors.\n//\n// In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but\n// using a gRPC stream to make it easier for the server to\n// maintain state.\n\nservice ExternalProcessor {\n  // This begins the bidirectional stream that Envoy will use to\n  // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\n  // protocol is described by the ProcessingRequest and ProcessingResponse\n  // messages below.\n  rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\n  }\n}\n\n// This represents the different types of messages that Envoy can send\n// to an external processing server.\n// [#next-free-field: 11]\nmessage ProcessingRequest {\n  reserved 1;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Each request message will include one of the following sub-messages. Which\n  // ones are set for a particular HTTP request/response depend on the\n  // processing mode.\n  oneof request {\n    option (validate.required) = true;\n\n    // Information about the HTTP request headers, as well as peer info and additional\n    // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\n    // HeaderResponse message, an ImmediateResponse message, or close the stream.\n    HttpHeaders request_headers = 2;\n\n    // Information about the HTTP response headers, as well as peer info and additional\n    // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\n    // HeaderResponse message or close the stream.\n    HttpHeaders response_headers = 3;\n\n    // A chunk of the HTTP request body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is true, the server must send back\n    // a BodyResponse message, an ImmediateResponse message, or close the stream.\n    HttpBody request_body = 4;\n\n    // A chunk of the HTTP response body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back\n    // a BodyResponse message or close the stream.\n    HttpBody response_body = 5;\n\n    // The HTTP trailers for the request path. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server\n    // must send back a TrailerResponse message or close the stream.\n    //\n    // This message is only sent if the trailers processing mode is set to ``SEND`` and\n    // the original downstream request has trailers.\n    HttpTrailers request_trailers = 6;\n\n    // The HTTP trailers for the response path. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server\n    // must send back a TrailerResponse message or close the stream.\n    //\n    // This message is only sent if the trailers processing mode is set to ``SEND`` and\n    // the original upstream response has trailers.\n    HttpTrailers response_trailers = 7;\n  }\n\n  // Dynamic metadata associated with the request.\n  config.core.v3.Metadata metadata_context = 8;\n\n  // The values of properties selected by the ``request_attributes``\n  // or ``response_attributes`` list in the configuration. Each entry\n  // in the list is populated from the standard\n  // :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>` supported across Envoy.\n  map<string, google.protobuf.Struct> attributes = 9;\n\n  // Specify whether the filter that sent this request is running in :ref:`observability_mode\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`\n  // and defaults to false.\n  //\n  // * A value of ``false`` indicates that the server must respond\n  //   to this message by either sending back a matching ProcessingResponse message,\n  //   or by closing the stream.\n  // * A value of ``true`` indicates that the server should not respond to this message, as any\n  //   responses will be ignored. However, it may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages\n  //   are needed.\n  //\n  bool observability_mode = 10;\n}\n\n// For every ProcessingRequest received by the server with the ``observability_mode`` field\n// set to false, the server must send back exactly one ProcessingResponse message.\n// [#next-free-field: 11]\nmessage ProcessingResponse {\n  oneof response {\n    option (validate.required) = true;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with the\n    // ``request_headers`` field set.\n    HeadersResponse request_headers = 1;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with the\n    // ``response_headers`` field set.\n    HeadersResponse response_headers = 2;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``request_body`` field set.\n    BodyResponse request_body = 3;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``response_body`` field set.\n    BodyResponse response_body = 4;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``request_trailers`` field set.\n    TrailersResponse request_trailers = 5;\n\n    // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\n    // the ``response_trailers`` field set.\n    TrailersResponse response_trailers = 6;\n\n    // If specified, attempt to create a locally generated response, send it\n    // downstream, and stop processing additional filters and ignore any\n    // additional messages received from the remote server for this request or\n    // response. If a response has already started -- for example, if this\n    // message is sent response to a ``response_body`` message -- then\n    // this will either ship the reply directly to the downstream codec,\n    // or reset the stream.\n    ImmediateResponse immediate_response = 7;\n  }\n\n  // Optional metadata that will be emitted as dynamic metadata to be consumed by\n  // following filters. This metadata will be placed in the namespace(s) specified by the top-level\n  // field name(s) of the struct.\n  google.protobuf.Struct dynamic_metadata = 8;\n\n  // Override how parts of the HTTP request and response are processed\n  // for the duration of this particular request/response only. Servers\n  // may use this to intelligently control how requests are processed\n  // based on the headers and other metadata that they see.\n  // This field is only applicable when servers responding to the header requests.\n  // If it is set in the response to the body or trailer requests, it will be ignored by Envoy.\n  // It is also ignored by Envoy when the ext_proc filter config\n  // :ref:`allow_mode_override\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.allow_mode_override>`\n  // is set to false.\n  envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode mode_override = 9;\n\n  // When ext_proc server receives a request message, in case it needs more\n  // time to process the message, it sends back a ProcessingResponse message\n  // with a new timeout value. When Envoy receives this response message,\n  // it ignores other fields in the response, just stop the original timer,\n  // which has the timeout value specified in\n  // :ref:`message_timeout\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n  // and start a new timer with this ``override_message_timeout`` value and keep the\n  // Envoy ext_proc filter state machine intact.\n  // Has to be >= 1ms and <=\n  // :ref:`max_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.max_message_timeout>`\n  // Such message can be sent at most once in a particular Envoy ext_proc filter processing state.\n  // To enable this API, one has to set ``max_message_timeout`` to a number >= 1ms.\n  google.protobuf.Duration override_message_timeout = 10;\n}\n\n// The following are messages that are sent to the server.\n\n// This message is sent to the external server when the HTTP request and responses\n// are first received.\nmessage HttpHeaders {\n  // The HTTP request headers. All header keys will be\n  // lower-cased, because HTTP header keys are case-insensitive.\n  // The ``headers`` encoding is based on the runtime guard\n  // envoy_reloadable_features_send_header_raw_value setting.\n  // When it is true, the header value is encoded in the\n  // :ref:`raw_value <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HeaderValue.raw_value>` field.\n  // When it is false, the header value is encoded in the\n  // :ref:`value <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HeaderValue.value>` field.\n  config.core.v3.HeaderMap headers = 1;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // This field is deprecated and not implemented. Attributes will be sent in\n  // the  top-level :ref:`attributes <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest.attributes`\n  // field.\n  map<string, google.protobuf.Struct> attributes = 2\n      [deprecated = true, (envoy.annotations.deprecated_at_minor_version) = \"3.0\"];\n\n  // If true, then there is no message body associated with this\n  // request or response.\n  bool end_of_stream = 3;\n}\n\n// This message contains the message body that Envoy sends to the external server.\nmessage HttpBody {\n  bytes body = 1;\n\n  bool end_of_stream = 2;\n}\n\n// This message contains the trailers.\nmessage HttpTrailers {\n  // The ``trailers`` encoding is based on the runtime guard\n  // envoy_reloadable_features_send_header_raw_value setting.\n  // When it is true, the header value is encoded in the\n  // :ref:`raw_value <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HeaderValue.raw_value>` field.\n  // When it is false, the header value is encoded in the\n  // :ref:`value <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HeaderValue.value>` field.\n  config.core.v3.HeaderMap trailers = 1;\n}\n\n// The following are messages that may be sent back by the server.\n\n// This message must be sent in response to an HttpHeaders message.\nmessage HeadersResponse {\n  CommonResponse response = 1;\n}\n\n// This message must be sent in response to an HttpTrailers message.\nmessage TrailersResponse {\n  // Instructions on how to manipulate the trailers\n  HeaderMutation header_mutation = 1;\n}\n\n// This message must be sent in response to an HttpBody message.\nmessage BodyResponse {\n  CommonResponse response = 1;\n}\n\n// This message contains common fields between header and body responses.\n// [#next-free-field: 6]\nmessage CommonResponse {\n  enum ResponseStatus {\n    // Apply the mutation instructions in this message to the\n    // request or response, and then continue processing the filter\n    // stream as normal. This is the default.\n    CONTINUE = 0;\n\n    // Apply the specified header mutation, replace the body with the body\n    // specified in the body mutation (if present), and do not send any\n    // further messages for this request or response even if the processing\n    // mode is configured to do so.\n    //\n    // When used in response to a request_headers or response_headers message,\n    // this status makes it possible to either completely replace the body\n    // while discarding the original body, or to add a body to a message that\n    // formerly did not have one.\n    //\n    // In other words, this response makes it possible to turn an HTTP GET\n    // into a POST, PUT, or PATCH.\n    CONTINUE_AND_REPLACE = 1;\n  }\n\n  // If set, provide additional direction on how the Envoy proxy should\n  // handle the rest of the HTTP filter chain.\n  ResponseStatus status = 1 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // Instructions on how to manipulate the headers. When responding to an\n  // HttpBody request, header mutations will only take effect if\n  // the current processing mode for the body is BUFFERED.\n  HeaderMutation header_mutation = 2;\n\n  // Replace the body of the last message sent to the remote server on this\n  // stream. Body mutations may take\n  // effect in response either to ``header`` or ``body`` messages. This is necessary\n  // if the remote server modified headers that are used to calculate the route.\n  // This field is ignored in the response direction. This field is also ignored\n  // if the Envoy ext_proc filter is in the upstream filter chain.\n  bool clear_route_cache = 5;\n}\n\n// This message causes the filter to attempt to create a locally\n// generated response, send it  downstream, stop processing\n// additional filters, and ignore any additional messages received\n// from the remote server for this request or response. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01CQ4A8hGrso4feNAWtk5zt1","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→.. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n     2→\n     3→External Processing\n     4→===================\n     5→* This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n     6→* :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n     7→\n     8→The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n     9→to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n    10→it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n    11→and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n    12→\n    13→The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    14→external processor\n    15→:ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    16→messages, and the processor must reply with\n    17→:ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n    18→messages.\n    19→\n    20→Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n    21→This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n    22→request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n    23→on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n    24→that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n    25→stream requests from the proxy.\n    26→\n    27→This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n    28→are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n    29→be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n    30→\n    31→Statistics\n    32→----------\n    33→This filter outputs statistics in the\n    34→``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n    35→<envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\n    36→comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n    37→\n    38→The following statistics are supported:\n    39→\n    40→.. csv-table::\n    41→  :header: Name, Type, Description\n    42→  :widths: auto\n    43→\n    44→  streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n    45→  streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n    46→  streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n    47→  spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n    48→  streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n    49→  streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n    50→  failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n    51→  message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n    52→  rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n    53→  clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n    54→  clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n    55→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
