The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\nit to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\nand modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n\nThe protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\nexternal processor\n:ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\nmessages, and the processor must reply with\n:ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\nmessages.\n\nConfiguration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\nThis way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\nrequest and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\non a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\nthat decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\nstream requests from the proxy.\n\nThis filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\nare complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\nbe found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n\nStatistics\n----------\nThis filter outputs statistics in the\n``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n<envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\ncomes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n\nThe following statistics are supported:\n\n.. csv-table::\n  :header: Name, Type, Description\n  :widths: auto\n\n  streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n  streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n  streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n  spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n  streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n  streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n  failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n  message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n  rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n  clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n  clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n","numLines":55,"startLine":1,"totalLines":55}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01K7iW4Z44ED652rxakUWyrw","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_012GnYQGj6MDHsskTUD7Kz5L","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide\n## Version 1.30.0 → 1.31.0\n\n## Overview\n\nThis guide documents the migration path for upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from version 1.30.0 (April 2024) to version 1.31.0 (July 2024).\n\nThe v1.31.0 release introduces significant improvements to observability mode and route cache management, while maintaining backward compatibility for most existing configurations. However, several important changes require attention:\n\n- **1 Breaking Change**: A field type change in the external processor response protocol\n- **1 Deprecated Field**: `disable_clear_route_cache` is superseded by a new enum-based `route_cache_action` field\n- **3 New Configuration Options**: Enhanced route cache control and stream lifecycle management\n- **Enhanced Observability Mode**: Improved support for non-blocking monitoring of traffic\n\nThe release focuses on improving observability mode with better stream lifecycle management and providing more granular control over route cache behavior.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. ImmediateResponse.body Field Type Change\n\n**Severity: High**\n**Impact: External Processor Implementations**\n\nThe `body` field in the `ImmediateResponse` message has changed from `string` to `bytes`.\n\n**Location**: `/api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`, Line 342\n\n#### Before (v1.30.0):\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  string body = 3;  // ← String type\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.31.0):\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  bytes body = 3;  // ← Bytes type\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Impact\n\nThis change affects any external processor implementation that sets the `body` field in an `ImmediateResponse`. The change from `string` to `bytes` means:\n\n1. **Binary Data Support**: The field can now properly handle arbitrary binary data, not just UTF-8 strings\n2. **Encoding Handling**: If your processor was sending UTF-8 text, you must now encode it to bytes explicitly\n\n#### Migration Steps for External Processors\n\n**Language-Specific Examples:**\n\n**Go:**\n```go\n// v1.30.0 (Old)\nresp := &service.ProcessingResponse{\n    Response: &service.ProcessingResponse_ImmediateResponse{\n        ImmediateResponse: &service.ImmediateResponse{\n            Status: &http_status.HttpStatus{Code: 403},\n            Body: \"Access Denied\",  // string\n        },\n    },\n}\n\n// v1.31.0 (New)\nresp := &service.ProcessingResponse{\n    Response: &service.ProcessingResponse_ImmediateResponse{\n        ImmediateResponse: &service.ImmediateResponse{\n            Status: &http_status.HttpStatus{Code: 403},\n            Body: []byte(\"Access Denied\"),  // bytes\n        },\n    },\n}\n```\n\n**Python:**\n```python\n# v1.30.0 (Old)\nresp = service_pb2.ProcessingResponse()\nresp.immediate_response.status.code = 403\nresp.immediate_response.body = \"Access Denied\"  # string\n\n# v1.31.0 (New)\nresp = service_pb2.ProcessingResponse()\nresp.immediate_response.status.code = 403\nresp.immediate_response.body = b\"Access Denied\"  # bytes\n```\n\n**C++:**\n```cpp\n// v1.30.0 (Old)\nauto* immediate_response = response.mutable_immediate_response();\nimmediate_response->mutable_status()->set_code(403);\nimmediate_response->set_body(\"Access Denied\");  // string\n\n// v1.31.0 (New)\nauto* immediate_response = response.mutable_immediate_response();\nimmediate_response->mutable_status()->set_code(403);\nimmediate_response->set_body(\"Access Denied\");  // bytes (auto-converts)\n```\n\n#### Validation\n\nTo ensure your external processor is compatible:\n\n1. Regenerate client/server stubs from the updated proto files\n2. Update all code that constructs `ImmediateResponse` messages\n3. Test with actual binary response bodies to verify correctness\n4. If using gRPC message encoding, the `grpc-message` header (for binary data) will now work correctly\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. disable_clear_route_cache Field\n\n**Status: Deprecated (not removed)**\n**Replacement: `route_cache_action` field**\n**Recommended Action: Migrate to the new `route_cache_action` field**\n\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field in the `ExternalProcessor` configuration message is superseded by the new `route_cache_action` enum field, which provides more granular control.\n\n**Location**: `/api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`, Lines 250-258\n\n#### Before (v1.30.0):\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // ... other fields ...\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.31.0):\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // ... other fields ...\n\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    DEFAULT = 0;   // Clear route cache based on clear_route_cache field\n    CLEAR = 1;     // Always clear the route cache\n    RETAIN = 2;    // Never clear the route cache\n  }\n\n  // Deprecated: Use route_cache_action instead\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // New: Recommended field for route cache control\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n}\n```\n\n#### Behavioral Equivalence\n\n- `disable_clear_route_cache: true` → `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- `disable_clear_route_cache: false` → `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n- New option → `route_cache_action: CLEAR` (always clear, no previous equivalent)\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n**YAML Configuration Migration:**\n\n**v1.30.0 Configuration:**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true  # ← Deprecated field\n```\n\n**v1.31.0 Configuration (Recommended):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # ← New field (recommended)\n```\n\n#### Constraints and Validation\n\nAs of v1.31.0, the Envoy filter validates that both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action` cannot be set to non-default values simultaneously. The validation logic (from `ext_proc.cc:218-221`):\n\n```cpp\nif (config.disable_clear_route_cache() &&\n    (route_cache_action_ !=\n     envoy::extensions::filters::http::ext_proc::v3::ExternalProcessor::DEFAULT)) {\n  throw EnvoyException(\"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not \"\n                       \"be set to none-default at the same time.\");\n}\n```\n\n**Valid Configuration Combinations:**\n- ✅ `disable_clear_route_cache: false` + `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n- ✅ `disable_clear_route_cache: false` + `route_cache_action: CLEAR`\n- ✅ `disable_clear_route_cache: true` + `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` (automatically converts to RETAIN)\n- ❌ `disable_clear_route_cache: true` + `route_cache_action: CLEAR` (invalid, throws error)\n- ❌ `disable_clear_route_cache: true` + `route_cache_action: RETAIN` (invalid, throws error)\n\n#### Automatic Migration\n\nIf you leave both fields unset, Envoy will use the default behavior. If you have only `disable_clear_route_cache: true`, the filter will automatically convert it to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`.\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Route Cache Action Enum (`route_cache_action`)\n\n**Introduced in v1.31.0**\n**Type**: `ExternalProcessor.RouteCacheAction` enum\n**Field Number**: 18\n**Default Value**: `DEFAULT`\n\nThis new field provides explicit control over when the route cache is cleared in response to external processor modifications of request headers.\n\n**Location**: `/api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`, Lines 103-120, 253-258\n\n#### Enum Values\n\n```protobuf\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // The default behavior: clear the route cache only when the\n  // clear_route_cache field is set in an external processor response.\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n  // the external processor response.\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Never clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n  // the external processor response. This is equivalent to setting\n  // disable_clear_route_cache to true.\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n```\n\n#### Use Cases\n\n| Value | Use Case | Example |\n|-------|----------|---------|\n| `DEFAULT` | Standard operation - external processor controls cache behavior | Most deployments; processor can request cache clear on demand |\n| `CLEAR` | Always recompute routes after external processing | Header manipulation that affects routing decisions is guaranteed |\n| `RETAIN` | Never clear route cache after external processing | External processor only modifies non-routing headers (e.g., authentication) |\n\n#### Configuration Examples\n\n**Example 1: Always Clear Route Cache**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n**Use When**: External processor modifies routing-affecting headers (e.g., `:authority`, custom routing headers) and you want to ensure routes are always recomputed.\n\n**Example 2: Never Clear Route Cache (Performance Optimization)**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n**Use When**: External processor only modifies headers that don't affect routing decisions (e.g., adding/removing authentication headers).\n\n**Example 3: Let External Processor Decide (Default)**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n**Use When**: Your external processor is intelligent enough to signal when route cache should be cleared via the `clear_route_cache` field in responses.\n\n#### Impact on Performance\n\n- **CLEAR mode**: Slight performance overhead due to route recomputation on every request\n- **RETAIN mode**: Potential for stale routing if processor modifies routing-affecting headers\n- **DEFAULT mode**: Balanced - only clears cache when necessary\n\n### 2. Deferred Close Timeout (`deferred_close_timeout`)\n\n**Introduced in v1.31.0**\n**Type**: `google.protobuf.Duration`\n**Field Number**: 19\n**Default Value**: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n**Applicable Mode**: Observability mode\n\nThis field controls how long the Envoy proxy will keep the gRPC stream to the external processor open after the main HTTP stream has closed, specifically in observability mode.\n\n**Location**: `/api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`, Lines 260-265\n\n#### Purpose\n\nIn observability mode, the external processor operates asynchronously:\n1. Envoy sends request/response data without waiting for processor responses\n2. The processor observes traffic for monitoring/analytics\n3. The main HTTP stream closes normally\n4. The observability stream may still have buffered data to process\n\nThe `deferred_close_timeout` ensures that:\n- The stream stays open long enough for buffered messages to be processed\n- Resources aren't wasted holding streams open indefinitely\n- The processor has predictable shutdown behavior\n\n#### Configuration Examples\n\n**Default Configuration (No explicit setting needed):**\n```yaml\n# Defaults to 5000ms\ngrpc_service:\n  envoy_grpc:\n    cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n```\n\n**Custom Timeout - Very Short (Eager Cleanup):**\n```yaml\ngrpc_service:\n  envoy_grpc:\n    cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\ndeferred_close_timeout: 1000ms  # 1 second\n```\n**Use When**: Resources are constrained and quick stream cleanup is important\n\n**Custom Timeout - Long (Ensure Processing Completes):**\n```yaml\ngrpc_service:\n  envoy_grpc:\n    cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\ndeferred_close_timeout: 30000ms  # 30 seconds\n```\n**Use When**: External processor has significant processing latency\n\n#### Important Notes\n\n1. **Only Applicable in Observability Mode**: This field is ignored unless `observability_mode: true`\n2. **Not a Request Timeout**: Different from `message_timeout`, which applies to synchronous processing\n3. **Graceful Shutdown**: Streams will close immediately if the processor closes its end first\n\n### 3. Enhanced Observability Mode Implementation\n\n**Introduced in v1.31.0**\n**Related Field**: `observability_mode` (existing in v1.30)\n\nThe observability mode has been significantly enhanced in v1.31.0 with proper stream lifecycle management and deferred closure support.\n\n#### What Changed\n\n**Filter Implementation** (`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`):\n\n1. **Thread-Local Stream Management**: Streams are now managed through a thread-local manager that handles stream storage and deferred cleanup\n   - Source: Lines 179-225 (new constructor), 320-325 (deferredCloseStream method)\n   - Benefit: Better lifecycle management and resource cleanup\n\n2. **Observability-Specific Methods**: New dedicated methods for observability mode:\n   - `sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()`: Lines 556-574\n   - `sendDataInObservabilityMode()`: Lines 576-619\n   - Benefit: Clear separation of observability vs. normal processing paths\n\n3. **Deferred Stream Closure**: In observability mode, streams now support deferred closure with a configurable timeout\n   - Source: Lines 320-325, 395-412\n   - Benefit: Prevents data loss when filter is destroyed before all observer messages are processed\n\n4. **Stream Lifecycle Tracking**:\n   - Streams track their IDs and can notify the filter of destruction\n   - The thread-local manager handles cleanup with optional deferred timeout\n   - Old behavior: Direct stream reset\n   - New behavior: Graceful deferred closure in observability mode\n\n#### Migration Impact for Observability Mode Users\n\n**If you're NOT using observability mode**: No action needed. These changes are transparent.\n\n**If you're using observability mode with `observability_mode: true`**:\n\n1. **Stream Closure Behavior Change**:\n   - **v1.30.0**: Streams closed immediately on filter destruction\n   - **v1.31.0**: Streams close gracefully with a deferred timeout (default 5 seconds)\n\n2. **Recommended Configuration**:\n   ```yaml\n   observability_mode: true\n   deferred_close_timeout: 5000ms  # Explicit (this is the default)\n   ```\n\n3. **Potential Issue**: If your external processor is slow to process buffered messages, you may see extended stream lifetimes. Adjust `deferred_close_timeout` accordingly:\n   ```yaml\n   observability_mode: true\n   deferred_close_timeout: 2000ms  # For faster cleanup if processor is fast\n   ```\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Updates\n\n### Summary of Configuration Changes\n\n| Feature | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 | Migration Required |\n|---------|---------|---------|-------------------|\n| Basic ext_proc | ✅ | ✅ | No |\n| `observability_mode` | ✅ | ✅ Improved | No (but behavior improved) |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | ✅ | ⚠️ Deprecated | Yes (replace with `route_cache_action`) |\n| `route_cache_action` | ❌ | ✅ New | Optional (but recommended) |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | ❌ | ✅ New | No (observability mode only) |\n| ImmediateResponse.body | `string` | `bytes` | Yes (for ext_proc implementations) |\n\n### Configuration Property Changes in FilterConfig\n\n**Implementation File**: `/source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h`\n\nThe internal `FilterConfig` class has changed to support the new features:\n\n**Removed Properties**:\n- `disable_clear_route_cache_` (replaced by `route_cache_action_`)\n\n**Added Properties**:\n- `observability_mode_` (boolean, copied from config)\n- `route_cache_action_` (enum RouteCacheAction)\n- `deferred_close_timeout_` (milliseconds duration)\n- `thread_local_stream_manager_slot_` (thread-local stream lifecycle management)\n\n**Accessor Methods Added**:\n```cpp\nbool observabilityMode() const;\nconst std::chrono::milliseconds& deferredCloseTimeout() const;\nRouteCacheAction routeCacheAction() const;\nThreadLocalStreamManager& threadLocalStreamManager() const;\n```\n\n### Breaking Configuration Requirements\n\n1. **If using `disable_clear_route_cache: true`**: Must migrate to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n2. **If sending `ImmediateResponse` messages**: Must update external processor to use `bytes` for body field\n3. **If using Envoy's gRPC client for ext_proc**: Stream options handling has changed (internal detail, transparent to users)\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Route Cache Management\n\n**Key Change**: More granular control with enum-based approach instead of boolean\n\n**Before (v1.30.0)**:\n- Route cache cleared only when external processor sets `clear_route_cache: true` in response\n- No way to force clearing or force retention\n\n**After (v1.31.0)**:\n- `DEFAULT`: Same as v1.30.0 (processor controls via response)\n- `CLEAR`: Always clear, regardless of processor response\n- `RETAIN`: Never clear, regardless of processor response\n\n**Implication**: You can now enforce consistent route cache behavior at the configuration level rather than relying on processor logic.\n\n### 2. Observability Mode Stream Lifecycle\n\n**Before (v1.30.0)**:\n```\nHTTP Request/Response → ext_proc stream open → filter destruction\n                           ↓                         ↓\n                        Processing        Stream closed immediately\n```\n\n**After (v1.31.0)**:\n```\nHTTP Request/Response → ext_proc stream open → filter destruction\n                           ↓                         ↓\n                        Processing        Deferred close (timeout-based)\n                                              ↓\n                                         Stream closed after timeout\n                                         or processor closes first\n```\n\n**Benefit**: Prevents data loss when filter is destroyed while processor is still handling buffered messages.\n\n**Caveat**: Stream resources may be held longer. Monitor with the new `deferred_close_timeout` setting.\n\n### 3. GRPC Stream Creation\n\n**Implementation Change** (`ext_proc.cc:338-349`):\n\nThe gRPC stream creation now includes additional context for better integration with Envoy's async client:\n\n**Before (v1.30.0)**:\n```cpp\nstream_ = client_->start(*this, config_with_hash_key_, decoder_callbacks_->streamInfo());\n```\n\n**After (v1.31.0)**:\n```cpp\nHttp::AsyncClient::ParentContext grpc_context;\ngrpc_context.stream_info = &decoder_callbacks_->streamInfo();\nauto options = Http::AsyncClient::StreamOptions()\n    .setParentSpan(decoder_callbacks_->activeSpan())\n    .setParentContext(grpc_context)\n    .setBufferBodyForRetry(true);\n\nExternalProcessorStreamPtr stream_object =\n    client_->start(*this, config_with_hash_key_, options, decoder_callbacks_);\n```\n\n**Benefit**: Better integration with tracing, parent context propagation, and connection reuse.\n\n**Impact**: Transparent to configuration; internal implementation detail.\n\n### 4. Stream Management via Thread-Local Storage\n\n**Implementation**: `ThreadLocalStreamManager` class added to handle stream lifecycle\n\n**What This Means**:\n- Streams are stored in thread-local storage for better lifecycle management\n- Deferred cleanup is now supported for observability mode\n- Stream IDs are tracked for proper resource cleanup\n\n**Implication**: If you've hooked into Envoy's internals, stream management has changed. This is typically transparent unless you have custom code interacting with ext_proc streams directly.\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Update External Processor Implementation (If Applicable)\n\nIf you have a custom external processor that generates `ImmediateResponse` messages:\n\n1. **Regenerate Proto Stubs**:\n   ```bash\n   # Download v1.31.0 API definitions\n   # Regenerate stubs for your language\n   protoc --go_out=. --go-grpc_out=. external_processor.proto  # Go example\n   ```\n\n2. **Update ImmediateResponse Handling**:\n   ```go\n   // Change from string to []byte\n   immediateResponse.Body = []byte(textContent)  // was: textContent\n   ```\n\n3. **Test Binary Response Bodies**:\n   ```go\n   // Test with actual bytes\n   immediateResponse.Body = []byte{0x89, 0x50, 0x4E, 0x47}  // PNG header\n   ```\n\n### Step 2: Update Envoy Configuration\n\n#### 2a. Update route_cache_control Strategy\n\n**Review Your Current Setting**:\n```yaml\n# Current configuration in v1.30.0\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Only option: true/false\n```\n\n**Update to v1.31.0**:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    # Replace disable_clear_route_cache with route_cache_action\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Use RETAIN instead of disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**Decision Tree for route_cache_action**:\n```\nDoes your external processor modify routing headers?\n├─ YES, always → route_cache_action: CLEAR\n├─ YES, sometimes → route_cache_action: DEFAULT (processor signals via clear_route_cache)\n└─ NO → route_cache_action: RETAIN (performance optimization)\n```\n\n#### 2b. If Using Observability Mode: Add deferred_close_timeout (Optional)\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n    # Optional: customize deferred close timeout (default is 5000ms)\n    deferred_close_timeout: 5000ms  # or adjust based on processor speed\n```\n\n### Step 3: Validation Before Upgrading\n\n1. **Check for disable_clear_route_cache Usage**:\n   ```bash\n   # Search all Envoy configs\n   grep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" .\n\n   # If found, plan migration\n   # true → change to route_cache_action: RETAIN\n   # false → change to route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n   ```\n\n2. **Test External Processor**:\n   ```bash\n   # Ensure external processor can handle bytes for body\n   # Test with: curl -X POST -d \"binary data\"\n   ```\n\n3. **Staging Environment Testing**:\n   - Deploy v1.31.0 Envoy with updated configuration\n   - Test normal request/response processing\n   - Test observability mode stream lifecycle (if applicable)\n   - Monitor stream count and deferred close behavior\n\n### Step 4: Deploy and Monitor\n\n1. **Pre-upgrade Checklist**:\n   - ✅ External processor updated to handle bytes body\n   - ✅ Envoy configuration updated (route_cache_action, deferred_close_timeout)\n   - ✅ Tests pass in staging\n   - ✅ Rollback plan documented\n\n2. **Deployment**:\n   - Deploy canary with small traffic percentage\n   - Monitor metrics:\n     - `ext_proc.streams_started`\n     - `ext_proc.clear_route_cache_ignored` (for RETAIN mode)\n     - `ext_proc.message_timeouts`\n   - Gradually increase traffic\n\n3. **Post-upgrade Verification**:\n   - Verify normal ext_proc processing continues\n   - Check observability mode stream behavior (if applicable)\n   - Monitor error rates and latency\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### Unit Tests for Configuration\n\n```yaml\n# Test case 1: route_cache_action RETAIN\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n# Verify: clear_route_cache from processor is ignored\n\n# Test case 2: route_cache_action CLEAR\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\n# Verify: route cache always cleared despite processor response\n\n# Test case 3: route_cache_action DEFAULT\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\n# Verify: processor clear_route_cache controls cache behavior\n```\n\n### Integration Tests\n\n**Test 1: ImmediateResponse with Binary Body**\n```\nScenario:\n1. External processor modifies routing headers\n2. Verify behavior matches route_cache_action setting\n3. HTTP request/response complete (main stream closes)\n2. Observability stream still has buffered messages\n3. Wait for deferred_close_timeout\n4. Stream closes and resources cleaned up\n\nExpected: Stream closes after timeout, no data loss\n```\n\n**Test 4: Backward Compatibility**\n```\nScenario:\n1. Load v1.30.0 configuration in v1.31.0 (with disable_clear_route_cache)\n2. Verify automatic conversion to route_cache_action\n\nExpected: Configuration loads successfully, behavior matches original\n```\n\n### Load Testing\n\n```\nBefore Migration:\n- Baseline metrics with v1.30.0\n- Message processing latency\n- Stream lifecycle metrics\n- GC pauses\n\nAfter Migration:\n- Compare message latency (should be same or better)\n- Verify stream closure behavior (deferred timeout working)\n- Check for memory leaks (streams properly cleaned)\n- Validate route cache impact on performance\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### Scenario 1: Configuration Errors\n\n**If you get error**: \"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time\"\n\n**Immediate Fix**:\n```bash\n# Revert configuration to remove conflicting settings\n# Option A: Use only route_cache_action\n# Option B: Use only disable_clear_route_cache (deprecated but still works)\n```\n\n### Scenario 2: External Processor Incompatibility\n\n**If external processor fails with message body parsing errors**:\n\n1. **Root Cause**: External processor not updated to handle bytes body type\n\n2. **Emergency Rollback Steps**:\n   ```bash\n   # 1. Immediately stop sending new requests to v1.31.0 Envoy\n   # 2. Route traffic back to v1.30.0 proxies\n   # 3. Update external processor proto stubs\n   # 4. Test with v1.31.0 again\n   ```\n\n3. **Verification**:\n   ```bash\n   # Test external processor with v1.31.0 proto definitions\n   # Verify binary body handling in logs\n   ```\n\n### Scenario 3: Observability Mode Stream Issues\n\n**If streams are held open too long**:\n\n1. **Symptom**: Resource exhaustion, file descriptor limits\n\n2. **Quick Fix**:\n   ```yaml\n   deferred_close_timeout: 1000ms  # Reduce from default 5000ms\n   ```\n\n3. **If that doesn't work**: Disable observability mode\n   ```yaml\n   observability_mode: false\n   ```\n\n### Scenario 4: Performance Degradation\n\n**If route cache behavior changed and routes are recomputed too frequently**:\n\n1. **Diagnostic**:\n   ```bash\n   # Check if using route_cache_action: CLEAR\n   # This forces route recomputation every request\n   ```\n\n2. **Fix**:\n   ```yaml\n   route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # or RETAIN if processor doesn't modify routing headers\n   ```\n\n### Full Rollback Procedure\n\n```bash\n# 1. Drain traffic from v1.31.0 Envoy instances\nenvoyctl drain <instance-id>\n\n# 2. Revert Envoy binary to v1.30.0\ndocker pull envoyproxy/envoy:v1.30-latest\nrestart_envoy_service\n\n# 3. Revert configuration to v1.30.0 format\n# Replace route_cache_action with disable_clear_route_cache\n\n# 4. However, several important changes require attention:\n\n- **1 Breaking Change**: A field type change in the external processor response protocol\n- **1 Deprecated Field**: `disable_clear_route_cache` is superseded by a new enum-based `route_cache_action` field\n- **3 New Configuration Options**: Enhanced route cache control and stream lifecycle management\n- **Enhanced Observability Mode**: Improved support for non-blocking monitoring of traffic\n\nThe release focuses on improving observability mode with better stream lifecycle management and providing more granular control over route cache behavior.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. ImmediateResponse.body Field Type Change\n\n**Severity: High**\n**Impact: External Processor Implementations**\n\nThe `body` field in the `ImmediateResponse` message has changed from `string` to `bytes`.\n\n**Location**: `/api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`, Line 342\n\n#### Before (v1.30.0):\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  string body = 3;  // ← String type\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.31.0):\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  bytes body = 3;  // ← Bytes type\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Impact\n\nThis change affects any external processor implementation that sets the `body` field in an `ImmediateResponse`. The change from `string` to `bytes` means:\n\n1. **Binary Data Support**: The field can now properly handle arbitrary binary data, not just UTF-8 strings\n2. **Encoding Handling**: If your processor was sending UTF-8 text, you must now encode it to bytes explicitly\n\n#### Migration Steps for External Processors\n\n**Language-Specific Examples:**\n\n**Go:**\n```go\n// v1.30.0 (Old)\nresp := &service.ProcessingResponse{\n    Response: &service.ProcessingResponse_ImmediateResponse{\n        ImmediateResponse: &service.ImmediateResponse{\n            Status: &http_status.HttpStatus{Code: 403},\n            Body: \"Access Denied\",  // string\n        },\n    },\n}\n\n// v1.31.0 (New)\nresp := &service.ProcessingResponse{\n    Response: &service.ProcessingResponse_ImmediateResponse{\n        ImmediateResponse: &service.ImmediateResponse{\n            Status: &http_status.HttpStatus{Code: 403},\n            Body: []byte(\"Access Denied\"),  // bytes\n        },\n    },\n}\n```\n\n**Python:**\n```python\n# v1.30.0 (Old)\nresp = service_pb2.ProcessingResponse()\nresp.immediate_response.status.code = 403\nresp.immediate_response.body = \"Access Denied\"  # string\n\n# v1.31.0 (New)\nresp = service_pb2.ProcessingResponse()\nresp.immediate_response.status.code = 403\nresp.immediate_response.body = b\"Access Denied\"  # bytes\n```\n\n**C++:**\n```cpp\n// v1.30.0 (Old)\nauto* immediate_response = response.mutable_immediate_response();\nimmediate_response->mutable_status()->set_code(403);\nimmediate_response->set_body(\"Access Denied\");  // string\n\n// v1.31.0 (New)\nauto* immediate_response = response.mutable_immediate_response();\nimmediate_response->mutable_status()->set_code(403);\nimmediate_response->set_body(\"Access Denied\");  // bytes (auto-converts)\n```\n\n#### Validation\n\nTo ensure your external processor is compatible:\n\n1. Regenerate client/server stubs from the updated proto files\n2. Update all code that constructs `ImmediateResponse` messages\n3. Test with actual binary response bodies to verify correctness\n4. If using gRPC message encoding, the `grpc-message` header (for binary data) will now work correctly\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. disable_clear_route_cache Field\n\n**Status: Deprecated (not removed)**\n**Replacement: `route_cache_action` field**\n**Recommended Action: Migrate to the new `route_cache_action` field**\n\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field in the `ExternalProcessor` configuration message is superseded by the new `route_cache_action` enum field, which provides more granular control.\n\n**Location**: `/api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`, Lines 250-258\n\n#### Before (v1.30.0):\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // ... other fields ...\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.31.0):\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // ... other fields ...\n\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    DEFAULT = 0;   // Clear route cache based on clear_route_cache field\n    CLEAR = 1;     // Always clear the route cache\n    RETAIN = 2;    // Never clear the route cache\n  }\n\n  // Deprecated: Use route_cache_action instead\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // New: Recommended field for route cache control\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n}\n```\n\n#### Behavioral Equivalence\n\n- `disable_clear_route_cache: true` → `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- `disable_clear_route_cache: false` → `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n- New option → `route_cache_action: CLEAR` (always clear, no previous equivalent)\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n**YAML Configuration Migration:**\n\n**v1.30.0 Configuration:**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true  # ← Deprecated field\n```\n\n**v1.31.0 Configuration (Recommended):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # ← New field (recommended)\n```\n\n#### Constraints and Validation\n\nAs of v1.31.0, the Envoy filter validates that both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action` cannot be set to non-default values simultaneously. The validation logic (from `ext_proc.cc:218-221`):\n\n```cpp\nif (config.disable_clear_route_cache() &&\n    (route_cache_action_ !=\n     envoy::extensions::filters::http::ext_proc::v3::ExternalProcessor::DEFAULT)) {\n  throw EnvoyException(\"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not \"\n                       \"be set to none-default at the same time.\");\n}\n```\n\n**Valid Configuration Combinations:**\n- ✅ `disable_clear_route_cache: false` + `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n- ✅ `disable_clear_route_cache: false` + `route_cache_action: CLEAR`\n- ✅ `disable_clear_route_cache: true` + `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` (automatically converts to RETAIN)\n- ❌ `disable_clear_route_cache: true` + `route_cache_action: CLEAR` (invalid, throws error)\n- ❌ `disable_clear_route_cache: true` + `route_cache_action: RETAIN` (invalid, throws error)\n\n#### Automatic Migration\n\nIf you leave both fields unset, Envoy will use the default behavior. If you have only `disable_clear_route_cache: true`, the filter will automatically convert it to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`.\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Route Cache Action Enum (`route_cache_action`)\n\n**Introduced in v1.31.0**\n**Type**: `ExternalProcessor.RouteCacheAction` enum\n**Field Number**: 18\n**Default Value**: `DEFAULT`\n\nThis new field provides explicit control over when the route cache is cleared in response to external processor modifications of request headers.\n\n**Location**: `/api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`, Lines 103-120, 253-258\n\n#### Enum Values\n\n```protobuf\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // The default behavior: clear the route cache only when the\n  // clear_route_cache field is set in an external processor response.\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n  // the external processor response.\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Never clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n  // the external processor response. This is equivalent to setting\n  // disable_clear_route_cache to true.\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n```\n\n#### Use Cases\n\n| Value | Use Case | Example |\n|-------|----------|---------|\n| `DEFAULT` | Standard operation - external processor controls cache behavior | Most deployments; processor can request cache clear on demand |\n| `CLEAR` | Always recompute routes after external processing | Header manipulation that affects routing decisions is guaranteed |\n| `RETAIN` | Never clear route cache after external processing | External processor only modifies non-routing headers (e.g., authentication) |\n\n#### Configuration Examples\n\n**Example 1: Always Clear Route Cache**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n**Use When**: External processor modifies routing-affecting headers (e.g., `:authority`, custom routing headers) and you want to ensure routes are always recomputed.\n\n**Example 2: Never Clear Route Cache (Performance Optimization)**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n**Use When**: External processor only modifies headers that don't affect routing decisions (e.g., adding/removing authentication headers).\n\n**Example 3: Let External Processor Decide (Default)**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n**Use When**: Your external processor is intelligent enough to signal when route cache should be cleared via the `clear_route_cache` field in responses.\n\n#### Impact on Performance\n\n- **CLEAR mode**: Slight performance overhead due to route recomputation on every request\n- **RETAIN mode**: Potential for stale routing if processor modifies routing-affecting headers\n- **DEFAULT mode**: Balanced - only clears cache when necessary\n\n### 2. Deferred Close Timeout (`deferred_close_timeout`)\n\n**Introduced in v1.31.0**\n**Type**: `google.protobuf.Duration`\n**Field Number**: 19\n**Default Value**: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n**Applicable Mode**: Observability mode\n\nThis field controls how long the Envoy proxy will keep the gRPC stream to the external processor open after the main HTTP stream has closed, specifically in observability mode.\n\n**Location**: `/api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`, Lines 260-265\n\n#### Purpose\n\nIn observability mode, the external processor operates asynchronously:\n1. Envoy sends request/response data without waiting for processor responses\n2. The processor observes traffic for monitoring/analytics\n3. The main HTTP stream closes normally\n4. The observability stream may still have buffered data to process\n\nThe `deferred_close_timeout` ensures that:\n- The stream stays open long enough for buffered messages to be processed\n- Resources aren't wasted holding streams open indefinitely\n- The processor has predictable shutdown behavior\n\n#### Configuration Examples\n\n**Default Configuration (No explicit setting needed):**\n```yaml\n# Defaults to 5000ms\ngrpc_service:\n  envoy_grpc:\n    cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n```\n\n**Custom Timeout - Very Short (Eager Cleanup):**\n```yaml\ngrpc_service:\n  envoy_grpc:\n    cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\ndeferred_close_timeout: 1000ms  # 1 second\n```\n**Use When**: Resources are constrained and quick stream cleanup is important\n\n**Custom Timeout - Long (Ensure Processing Completes):**\n```yaml\ngrpc_service:\n  envoy_grpc:\n    cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\ndeferred_close_timeout: 30000ms  # 30 seconds\n```\n**Use When**: External processor has significant processing latency\n\n#### Important Notes\n\n1. **Only Applicable in Observability Mode**: This field is ignored unless `observability_mode: true`\n2. **Not a Request Timeout**: Different from `message_timeout`, which applies to synchronous processing\n3. **Graceful Shutdown**: Streams will close immediately if the processor closes its end first\n\n### 3. Enhanced Observability Mode Implementation\n\n**Introduced in v1.31.0**\n**Related Field**: `observability_mode` (existing in v1.30)\n\nThe observability mode has been significantly enhanced in v1.31.0 with proper stream lifecycle management and deferred closure support.\n\n#### What Changed\n\n**Filter Implementation** (`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`):\n\n1. **Thread-Local Stream Management**: Streams are now managed through a thread-local manager that handles stream storage and deferred cleanup\n   - Source: Lines 179-225 (new constructor), 320-325 (deferredCloseStream method)\n   - Benefit: Better lifecycle management and resource cleanup\n\n2. **Observability-Specific Methods**: New dedicated methods for observability mode:\n   - `sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()`: Lines 556-574\n   - `sendDataInObservabilityMode()`: Lines 576-619\n   - Benefit: Clear separation of observability vs. normal processing paths\n\n3. **Deferred Stream Closure**: In observability mode, streams now support deferred closure with a configurable timeout\n   - Source: Lines 320-325, 395-412\n   - Benefit: Prevents data loss when filter is destroyed before all observer messages are processed\n\n4. **Stream Lifecycle Tracking**:\n   - Streams track their IDs and can notify the filter of destruction\n   - The thread-local manager handles cleanup with optional deferred timeout\n   - Old behavior: Direct stream reset\n   - New behavior: Graceful deferred closure in observability mode\n\n#### Migration Impact for Observability Mode Users\n\n**If you're NOT using observability mode**: No action needed. These changes are transparent.\n\n**If you're using observability mode with `observability_mode: true`**:\n\n1. **Stream Closure Behavior Change**:\n   - **v1.30.0**: Streams closed immediately on filter destruction\n   - **v1.31.0**: Streams close gracefully with a deferred timeout (default 5 seconds)\n\n2. **Recommended Configuration**:\n   ```yaml\n   observability_mode: true\n   deferred_close_timeout: 5000ms  # Explicit (this is the default)\n   ```\n\n3. **Potential Issue**: If your external processor is slow to process buffered messages, you may see extended stream lifetimes. Adjust `deferred_close_timeout` accordingly:\n   ```yaml\n   observability_mode: true\n   deferred_close_timeout: 2000ms  # For faster cleanup if processor is fast\n   ```\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Updates\n\n### Summary of Configuration Changes\n\n| Feature | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 | Migration Required |\n|---------|---------|---------|-------------------|\n| Basic ext_proc | ✅ | ✅ | No |\n| `observability_mode` | ✅ | ✅ Improved | No (but behavior improved) |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | ✅ | ⚠️ Deprecated | Yes (replace with `route_cache_action`) |\n| `route_cache_action` | ❌ | ✅ New | Optional (but recommended) |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | ❌ | ✅ New | No (observability mode only) |\n| ImmediateResponse.body | `string` | `bytes` | Yes (for ext_proc implementations) |\n\n### Configuration Property Changes in FilterConfig\n\n**Implementation File**: `/source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h`\n\nThe internal `FilterConfig` class has changed to support the new features:\n\n**Removed Properties**:\n- `disable_clear_route_cache_` (replaced by `route_cache_action_`)\n\n**Added Properties**:\n- `observability_mode_` (boolean, copied from config)\n- `route_cache_action_` (enum RouteCacheAction)\n- `deferred_close_timeout_` (milliseconds duration)\n- `thread_local_stream_manager_slot_` (thread-local stream lifecycle management)\n\n**Accessor Methods Added**:\n```cpp\nbool observabilityMode() const;\nconst std::chrono::milliseconds& deferredCloseTimeout() const;\nRouteCacheAction routeCacheAction() const;\nThreadLocalStreamManager& threadLocalStreamManager() const;\n```\n\n### Breaking Configuration Requirements\n\n1. **If using `disable_clear_route_cache: true`**: Must migrate to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n2. **If sending `ImmediateResponse` messages**: Must update external processor to use `bytes` for body field\n3. **If using Envoy's gRPC client for ext_proc**: Stream options handling has changed (internal detail, transparent to users)\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Route Cache Management\n\n**Key Change**: More granular control with enum-based approach instead of boolean\n\n**Before (v1.30.0)**:\n- Route cache cleared only when external processor sets `clear_route_cache: true` in response\n- No way to force clearing or force retention\n\n**After (v1.31.0)**:\n- `DEFAULT`: Same as v1.30.0 (processor controls via response)\n- `CLEAR`: Always clear, regardless of processor response\n- `RETAIN`: Never clear, regardless of processor response\n\n**Implication**: You can now enforce consistent route cache behavior at the configuration level rather than relying on processor logic.\n\n### 2. Observability Mode Stream Lifecycle\n\n**Before (v1.30.0)**:\n```\nHTTP Request/Response → ext_proc stream open → filter destruction\n                           ↓                         ↓\n                        Processing        Stream closed immediately\n```\n\n**After (v1.31.0)**:\n```\nHTTP Request/Response → ext_proc stream open → filter destruction\n                           ↓                         ↓\n                        Processing        Deferred close (timeout-based)\n                                              ↓\n                                         Stream closed after timeout\n                                         or processor closes first\n```\n\n**Benefit**: Prevents data loss when filter is destroyed while processor is still handling buffered messages.\n\n**Caveat**: Stream resources may be held longer. Monitor with the new `deferred_close_timeout` setting.\n\n### 3. GRPC Stream Creation\n\n**Implementation Change** (`ext_proc.cc:338-349`):\n\nThe gRPC stream creation now includes additional context for better integration with Envoy's async client:\n\n**Before (v1.30.0)**:\n```cpp\nstream_ = client_->start(*this, config_with_hash_key_, decoder_callbacks_->streamInfo());\n```\n\n**After (v1.31.0)**:\n```cpp\nHttp::AsyncClient::ParentContext grpc_context;\ngrpc_context.stream_info = &decoder_callbacks_->streamInfo();\nauto options = Http::AsyncClient::StreamOptions()\n    .setParentSpan(decoder_callbacks_->activeSpan())\n    .setParentContext(grpc_context)\n    .setBufferBodyForRetry(true);\n\nExternalProcessorStreamPtr stream_object =\n    client_->start(*this, config_with_hash_key_, options, decoder_callbacks_);\n```\n\n**Benefit**: Better integration with tracing, parent context propagation, and connection reuse.\n\n**Impact**: Transparent to configuration; internal implementation detail.\n\n### 4. Stream Management via Thread-Local Storage\n\n**Implementation**: `ThreadLocalStreamManager` class added to handle stream lifecycle\n\n**What This Means**:\n- Streams are stored in thread-local storage for better lifecycle management\n- Deferred cleanup is now supported for observability mode\n- Stream IDs are tracked for proper resource cleanup\n\n**Implication**: If you've hooked into Envoy's internals, stream management has changed. This is typically transparent unless you have custom code interacting with ext_proc streams directly.\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Update External Processor Implementation (If Applicable)\n\nIf you have a custom external processor that generates `ImmediateResponse` messages:\n\n1. **Regenerate Proto Stubs**:\n   ```bash\n   # Download v1.31.0 API definitions\n   # Regenerate stubs for your language\n   protoc --go_out=. --go-grpc_out=. external_processor.proto  # Go example\n   ```\n\n2. **Update ImmediateResponse Handling**:\n   ```go\n   // Change from string to []byte\n   immediateResponse.Body = []byte(textContent)  // was: textContent\n   ```\n\n3. **Test Binary Response Bodies**:\n   ```go\n   // Test with actual bytes\n   immediateResponse.Body = []byte{0x89, 0x50, 0x4E, 0x47}  // PNG header\n   ```\n\n### Step 2: Update Envoy Configuration\n\n#### 2a. Update route_cache_control Strategy\n\n**Review Your Current Setting**:\n```yaml\n# Current configuration in v1.30.0\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Only option: true/false\n```\n\n**Update to v1.31.0**:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    # Replace disable_clear_route_cache with route_cache_action\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Use RETAIN instead of disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**Decision Tree for route_cache_action**:\n```\nDoes your external processor modify routing headers?\n├─ YES, always → route_cache_action: CLEAR\n├─ YES, sometimes → route_cache_action: DEFAULT (processor signals via clear_route_cache)\n└─ NO → route_cache_action: RETAIN (performance optimization)\n```\n\n#### 2b. If Using Observability Mode: Add deferred_close_timeout (Optional)\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n    # Optional: customize deferred close timeout (default is 5000ms)\n    deferred_close_timeout: 5000ms  # or adjust based on processor speed\n```\n\n### Step 3: Validation Before Upgrading\n\n1. **Check for disable_clear_route_cache Usage**:\n   ```bash\n   # Search all Envoy configs\n   grep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" .\n\n   # If found, plan migration\n   # true → change to route_cache_action: RETAIN\n   # false → change to route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n   ```\n\n2. **Test External Processor**:\n   ```bash\n   # Ensure external processor can handle bytes for body\n   # Test with: curl -X POST -d \"binary data\"\n   ```\n\n3. **Staging Environment Testing**:\n   - Deploy v1.31.0 Envoy with updated configuration\n   - Test normal request/response processing\n   - Test observability mode stream lifecycle (if applicable)\n   - Monitor stream count and deferred close behavior\n\n### Step 4: Deploy and Monitor\n\n1. **Pre-upgrade Checklist**:\n   - ✅ External processor updated to handle bytes body\n   - ✅ Envoy configuration updated (route_cache_action, deferred_close_timeout)\n   - ✅ Tests pass in staging\n   - ✅ Rollback plan documented\n\n2. **Deployment**:\n   - Deploy canary with small traffic percentage\n   - Monitor metrics:\n     - `ext_proc.streams_started`\n     - `ext_proc.clear_route_cache_ignored` (for RETAIN mode)\n     - `ext_proc.message_timeouts`\n   - Gradually increase traffic\n\n3. **Post-upgrade Verification**:\n   - Verify normal ext_proc processing continues\n   - Check observability mode stream behavior (if applicable)\n   - Monitor error rates and latency\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### Unit Tests for Configuration\n\n```yaml\n# Test case 1: route_cache_action RETAIN\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n# Verify: clear_route_cache from processor is ignored\n\n# Test case 2: route_cache_action CLEAR\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\n# Verify: route cache always cleared despite processor response\n\n# Test case 3: route_cache_action DEFAULT\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\n# Verify: processor clear_route_cache controls cache behavior\n```\n\n### Integration Tests\n\n**Test 1: ImmediateResponse with Binary Body**\n```\nScenario:\n1. External processor returns ImmediateResponse with binary body (bytes)\n2. Envoy sends response to client\n3. Client receives exact binary content\n\nExpected: Binary content is preserved without encoding issues\n```\n\n**Test 2: Route Cache Behavior**\n```\nScenario:\n1. External processor modifies routing headers\n2. Verify behavior matches route_cache_action setting\n3. Check that routes are recomputed (CLEAR) or cached (RETAIN)\n\nExpected: Route decisions align with route_cache_action setting\n```\n\n**Test 3: Observability Mode Stream Closure**\n```\nScenario:\n1. HTTP request/response complete (main stream closes)\n2. Observability stream still has buffered messages\n3. Wait for deferred_close_timeout\n4. Stream closes and resources cleaned up\n\nExpected: Stream closes after timeout, no data loss\n```\n\n**Test 4: Backward Compatibility**\n```\nScenario:\n1. Load v1.30.0 configuration in v1.31.0 (with disable_clear_route_cache)\n2. Verify automatic conversion to route_cache_action\n\nExpected: Configuration loads successfully, behavior matches original\n```\n\n### Load Testing\n\n```\nBefore Migration:\n- Baseline metrics with v1.30.0\n- Message processing latency\n- Stream lifecycle metrics\n- GC pauses\n\nAfter Migration:\n- Compare message latency (should be same or better)\n- Verify stream closure behavior (deferred timeout working)\n- Check for memory leaks (streams properly cleaned)\n- Validate route cache impact on performance\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### Scenario 1: Configuration Errors\n\n**If you get error**: \"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time\"\n\n**Immediate Fix**:\n```bash\n# Revert configuration to remove conflicting settings\n# Option A: Use only route_cache_action\n# Option B: Use only disable_clear_route_cache (deprecated but still works)\n```\n\n### Scenario 2: External Processor Incompatibility\n\n**If external processor fails with message body parsing errors**:\n\n1. **Root Cause**: External processor not updated to handle bytes body type\n\n2. **Emergency Rollback Steps**:\n   ```bash\n   # 1. Immediately stop sending new requests to v1.31.0 Envoy\n   # 2. Route traffic back to v1.30.0 proxies\n   # 3. Update external processor proto stubs\n   # 4. Test with v1.31.0 again\n   ```\n\n3. **Verification**:\n   ```bash\n   # Test external processor with v1.31.0 proto definitions\n   # Verify binary body handling in logs\n   ```\n\n### Scenario 3: Observability Mode Stream Issues\n\n**If streams are held open too long**:\n\n1. **Symptom**: Resource exhaustion, file descriptor limits\n\n2. **Quick Fix**:\n   ```yaml\n   deferred_close_timeout: 1000ms  # Reduce from default 5000ms\n   ```\n\n3. **If that doesn't work**: Disable observability mode\n   ```yaml\n   observability_mode: false\n   ```\n\n### Scenario 4: Performance Degradation\n\n**If route cache behavior changed and routes are recomputed too frequently**:\n\n1. **Diagnostic**:\n   ```bash\n   # Check if using route_cache_action: CLEAR\n   # This forces route recomputation every request\n   ```\n\n2. **Fix**:\n   ```yaml\n   route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # or RETAIN if processor doesn't modify routing headers\n   ```\n\n### Full Rollback Procedure\n\n```bash\n# 1. Drain traffic from v1.31.0 Envoy instances\nenvoyctl drain <instance-id>\n\n# 2. Revert Envoy binary to v1.30.0\ndocker pull envoyproxy/envoy:v1.30-latest\nrestart_envoy_service\n\n# 3. Revert configuration to v1.30.0 format\n# Replace route_cache_action with disable_clear_route_cache\n\n# 4. Revert external processor to v1.30.0 proto definitions\n# Rebuild external processor with old proto stubs\n\n# 5. Verify operation\ncurl -v http://proxy:8000/test_endpoint\n\n# 6. Monitor error rates for 10 minutes\n# If stable, migration can be reattempted after fixes\n```\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: Proto File Locations and Changes\n\n### Modified Proto Files\n\n#### 1.
